### Post by ubuntu-geek on 2007-04-16
From: [http://www.ubuntu.com/news/ubuntu704](http://www.ubuntu.com/news/ubuntu704)

> **Latest Ubuntu delivers on the promise of Open Source**

 ***While millions consider whether to pay for Vista, the Ubuntu project releases its secure, high performance, free desktop and server editions.***
  
 LONDON, April 16, 2007 – For users wanting a secure, feature rich alternative to Microsoft Windows, Canonical Ltd., the commercial sponsor of Ubuntu, announced today the Thursday release of Ubuntu version 7.04. 
 Ubuntu is the award-winning [Linux distribution for the desktop]("http://www.ubuntu.com/news/ubuntudesktop704"), laptop, thin client and [server]("http://www.ubuntu.com/news/ubuntuserver704") which brings together the best of open source software every 6 months. Ubuntu 7.04 desktop edition includes a ground-breaking Windows migration assistant, excellent wireless networking support and improved multimedia support.
 [Ubuntu 7.04 server edition]("http://www.ubuntu.com/news/ubuntuserver704") adds support for hardware facilities that speed up the use of virtual machines as well as other improved hardware support, making it an excellent choice as a web, database, file and print server, the fastest growing area of Linux server use. Ubuntu's already outstanding support for thin clients is boosted with advanced print and sound support. 
 "In the coming months, many individuals and businesses will be making the decision to upgrade their existing computer systems and their operating systems," said Jane Silber, director of Operations, Canonical Ltd. "With added features to both the desktop and server editions, Ubuntu 7.04 is the most user-friendly version to date and is ideally suited to anyone who wants to make the switch to Linux and join the community of Ubuntu users. In fact, with this version of Ubuntu, it is easier than ever to move away from proprietary platforms."
 At the same time as Ubuntu, the project also will release new versions of [Kubuntu and Edubuntu]("http://www.ubuntu.com/news/ubuntuflavours704"), specialized versions of Ubuntu which include the KDE desktop environment and educational applications, respectively.
 **Ubuntu Fully Supported**

 Used by businesses, home users, schools and governments around the world, upgrades to new releases will always be free of charge. Ubuntu 7.04 will be maintained for 18 months on both the desktop and on the server, and additional free support is available from the thriving Ubuntu community. For deployments which require additional service guarantees, full telephone and online support is commercially available globally from the professional support team at Canonical Ltd and service partners.
  
 **About Canonical and Ubuntu**

 Canonical, the commercial sponsor of Ubuntu, is headquartered in Europe and is committed to the development, distribution and support of open source software products and communities. World-class 24x7 commercial support for Ubuntu is available through Canonical's global support team and partners. Since its launch in October 2004 Ubuntu has become one of the most highly regarded Linux distributions with millions of users around the world. Ubuntu will always be free to download, free to use and free to distribute to others. With these goals in mind, Ubuntu aims to be the most widely used Linux system, and is the centre of a global open source software ecosystem.
 Download Ubuntu from [www.ubuntu.com/download]("http://www.ubuntu.com/download"). To learn about commercial support for Ubuntu, Kubuntu and Edubuntu, please see [www.canonical.com/support]("http://www.canonical.com/support"). For more information visit [www.canonical.com]("http://www.canonical.com/") or [www.ubuntu.com]("http://www.ubuntu.com/").
 ###
 Ubuntu, Kubuntu, Edubuntu and their associated logos are all registered trademarks of Canonical Ltd.
 Contact:
Bill Baker, Baker Communications Group, 860-350-9100, [EMAIL="pr@canonical.com"]pr@canonical.com[/EMAIL]

### Post by ebozzz on 2007-04-16
> **onlybui said:**
> Wonder if the upgrade will work flawlessly...

I don't know about *flawlessly*. I have Feisty on all of my desktops already. One of them broke and I had to do a re-install. Two of them have an issue with the *search* magnifying glass appearing on the panel once they boot to the desktop. Not a big issue but I prefer that it didn't happen. One is just fine or so it seems. The last was a clean install that has been fine.  

On the ones that I had problems I used the command

```
gksu "update-manager -c -d"
```. 

You can also run 

```
sudo apt-get dist-upgrade
```.

So, beware if you have important files that cannot be lost. I had everything that I needed backed up.

---

### Post by msak007 on 2007-04-17
> **saxsux said:**
> Just wondering, when will Fiesty be supported until?
Will there eventually be another LTS release, once Dapper becomes unsupported in 2009?
Mark Shuttleworth himself said Gutsy (7.10) won't be LTS, but gave no indication as to which version would be. But according to an [interview with Jonathan Riddell]("http://www.kubuntu-de.org/interview-mit-riddell-zu-kde4-englisch") (Kubuntu lead dev) when asked about whether KDE 4.0 would be the default DE for Kubuntu 7.10 (as KDE4 is scheduled for release in October as well), he hinted that it would neither be the default for 7.10 (as it would probably not be stable enough), nor would it be the default for 8.04 because that would most likely be the next LTS. That's the only info I've been able to find regarding which version will be the next LTS, but that seems very likely.

### Post by teddybairs1 on 2007-04-18
I know this has already been answered a hundred times, but it keeps getting asked. If you've kept up with the update managers then you will already have the release version of Feisty come Thursday if you're already been running Feisty as a beta. If you're running edgy, you should probably be ok with doing the distribution upgrade if you don't have a lot of tweaking or programs already on your system. If you're running dapper, you must upgrade to edgy to upgrade to feisty, or else you must do a clean install from a disk. 

I tried the distro-upgrade to the Feisty beta and broke my system in the process when the upgrade manager hung after it was almost done. But with my system it had to download nearly two gigabytes of software because that's how many packages I had on my system. The normal download should be around 697MB. 

If you think it might kill your system with the distro upgrade do this: 1)burn a fresh copy of the Feisty .iso, 2)burn all of your personal files (important and otherwise) onto a backup cd/dvd, be sure to include any packages or programs that you had to install independent of the repos, and 3)once all this is done, try the distro upgrade anyway. If it works, then it should keep all of your settings and preferences. If it hangs and trashes your system, then you have the iso and backup disks and should be able to recover everything within a few hours. If you have a dual boot system, like I do, there are programs like ext2fs which will allow your windows xp os see your linux partitions and import files from them. One trick I do is use my windows drive to recover my personal files from the linux partition if for any reason I can't boot into it. Remember, just because you can't boot into a partition doesn't mean that your files are lost.

Hope this helps and answers some questions.

---

### Post by markl187ld on 2007-04-18
> **tdlrali said:**
> What does the about window say?

This version (Feisty Fawn) was released in April 2007 so its version number is 7.04.

```
mark@Lin:~$ cat /etc/issue
Ubuntu 7.04 \n \l

mark@Lin:~$ lsb_release -a
No LSB modules are available.
Distributor ID: Ubuntu
Description:    Ubuntu 7.04
Release:        7.04
Codename:       feisty
mark@Lin:~$ 

```

### Post by chakkaradeep on 2007-04-18
From your Dapper terminal, please do,

**sudo update-manager -d -c**

It will show that Edgy Eft is available and please first upgrade to Edgy.

From Edgy do the same thing,

**sudo udate-manager -d -c**

And you will have Feisty Fawn !

IT IS NOT ADVISED TO DIRECTLY UPGRADE TO FEISTY FROM DAPPER

---

[http://cdimage.ubuntu.com/daily-live/current/MD5SUMS](http://cdimage.ubuntu.com/daily-live/current/MD5SUMS)

---

You do know that they put data on the FTP in advance, right? And then move it to the appropriate folder on release. The reason the file has the same date/sum as the RC is because when a RC is accepted as releaseable they just use the same image file for the gold release.

### Post by HotShotDJ on 2007-04-19
Waiting for 7.04
> 
ESTRAGON:
    You say we have to come back tomorrow? 
VLADIMIR:
    Yes. 
ESTRAGON:
    Then we can bring a good bit of rope. 
VLADIMIR:
    Yes. 
    Silence. 
ESTRAGON:
    Didi? 
VLADIMIR:
    Yes. 
ESTRAGON:
    I can't go on like this. 
VLADIMIR:
    That's what you think. 
ESTRAGON:
    If we parted? That might be better for us. 
VLADIMIR:
    We'll hang ourselves tomorrow. (Pause.) Unless 7.04 comes. 
ESTRAGON:
    And if he comes? 
VLADIMIR:
    We'll be saved. 
    Vladimir takes off his hat (Lucky's), peers inside it, feels about inside it, shakes it, knocks on the crown, puts it on again. 
ESTRAGON:
    Well? Shall we go? 
VLADIMIR:
    Pull on your trousers. 
ESTRAGON:
    What? 
VLADIMIR:
    Pull on your trousers. 
ESTRAGON:
    You want me to pull off my trousers? 
VLADIMIR:
    Pull ON your trousers. 
ESTRAGON:
    (realizing his trousers are down). True. 
    He pulls up his trousers. 
VLADIMIR:
    Well? Shall we go? 
ESTRAGON:
    Yes, let's go. 
    They do not move.

### Post by jdb3654 on 2007-04-19
What is the difference between the dvd install and the cd install?  Should I waste my time downloading the dvd?

---

### Post by elyk on 2007-04-19
I think the DVD includes both Live CD and alternate install methods; cd just includes one. Unless you've got very little ram (like less than 128 mb) or have some other reason to use the alternate install, I'd recommend you just get the CD install
> Well if the servers have copies already, they are doing one heck of a good job at hidden the ISO's  
It's not that hard really; just turn off directory indexing and put the files somewhere that they won't be easily guessed. Then, when you're ready to release, just move the file to the main download directory, and add the link from the homepage.
Or (simpler), just upload it to the download directory, then add the link as soon as the upload finishes (if that's the case, it could be uploading as we post)
> with the hype .. the servers might crash.. this looks bigger than the wii , ps2 and the xbox 360 put together!!
That's why everyone who can should download using bittorrent...with all the hype this is getting, there should be enough peers for nice fast download speeds. I wonder how long until they figure out how to deliver apt upgrades with bittorrent (electricsheep did it with their latest screensaver)

### Post by Speque on 2007-04-19
> **ericesque said:**
> don't you mean iRock Cast?  I believe Apple invented iRC

IRC was invented in Finland by a Finnish student. \o/ 

Wikipedia knows:

"Internet Relay Chat (IRC) is a form of real-time Internet chat or synchronous conferencing. It is mainly designed for group (many-to-many) communication in discussion forums called channels, but also allows one-to-one communication and data transfers via private message.

IRC was created by Jarkko "WiZ" Oikarinen in late August 1988 to replace a program called MUT (MultiUser talk) on a BBS called OuluBox in Finland. Oikarinen found inspiration in a chat system known as Bitnet Relay, which operated on the BITNET.

IRC gained prominence when it was used to report on the Soviet coup attempt of 1991 throughout a media blackout. It was previously used in a similar fashion by Kuwaitis during the Iraqi invasion. Relevant logs are available from ibiblio archive.

IRC client software is available for virtually every computer operating system."

### Post by Takasho on 2007-04-19
ITS DELAYED!

The release Date for Ubuntu Feisty Fawn has been delayed due to validation bugs, There is no ETA yet, but the Ubuntu team hopes the delay will be just a few days.

Here the complete note:
"The Ubuntu 7.04 release candidate (due today) has been delayed due to
bugs discovered during validation testing, specifically problems with
certain ATA chipsets and problems with the connection status displayed
by the network-manager panel applet. There is no updated ETA yet, but
the core development team is actively working on the problems and expect
it to be a matter of days.

We'll put out a further announcement when more is known, and in the
meantime we ask our testing community to stay alert for notices of
specific changes that need to be tested.

Thanks,

--
Colin Watson"

### Post by teutatis on 2007-04-19
> **Takasho said:**
> ITS DELAYED!

The release Date for Ubuntu Feisty Fawn has been delayed due to validation bugs, There is no ETA yet, but the Ubuntu team hopes the delay will be just a few days.

Here the complete note:
"The Ubuntu 7.04 release candidate (due today) has been delayed due to
bugs discovered during validation testing, specifically problems with
certain ATA chipsets and problems with the connection status displayed
by the network-manager panel applet. There is no updated ETA yet, but
the core development team is actively working on the problems and expect
it to be a matter of days.

We'll put out a further announcement when more is known, and in the
meantime we ask our testing community to stay alert for notices of
specific changes that need to be tested.

Thanks,

--
Colin Watson"

this is not fun, not after 10 hours waiting for the final

### Post by enthusaroo on 2007-04-19
While we have a moment. I'd like to turn your attention to something a little bit serious for just a moment...

Hamburger holds that we have to choose between deconstructivist subdialectic theory and constructive rationalism. It could be said that the main theme of the works of Smith is the fatal flaw of neocultural consciousness. Many appropriations concerning the difference between sexual identity and society may be revealed. It could be said that the main theme of d’Erlette’s analysis of predialectic rationalism is the role of the writer as reader. Sontag uses the term ‘dialectic post textual theory’ to denote not discourse per se, but neodiscourse. Therefore, the subject is contextualized into a semanticist paradigm of expression that includes consciousness as a whole. 

Your thoughts?

---

> While we have a moment. I'd like to turn your attention to something a little bit serious for just a moment...

Hamburger holds that we have to choose between deconstructivist subdialectic theory and constructive rationalism. It could be said that the main theme of the works of Smith is the fatal flaw of neocultural consciousness. Many appropriations concerning the difference between sexual identity and society may be revealed. It could be said that the main theme of d’Erlette’s analysis of predialectic rationalism is the role of the writer as reader. Sontag uses the term ‘dialectic post textual theory’ to denote not discourse per se, but neodiscourse. Therefore, the subject is contextualized into a semanticist paradigm of expression that includes consciousness as a whole. 

Your thoughts?

Thanks,

Colin Watson"

### Post by Rtax on 2007-04-19
> **enthusaroo said:**
> While we have a moment. I'd like to turn your attention to something a little bit serious for just a moment...

Hamburger holds that we have to choose between deconstructivist subdialectic theory and constructive rationalism. It could be said that the main theme of the works of Smith is the fatal flaw of neocultural consciousness. Many appropriations concerning the difference between sexual identity and society may be revealed. It could be said that the main theme of d’Erlette’s analysis of predialectic rationalism is the role of the writer as reader. Sontag uses the term ‘dialectic post textual theory’ to denote not discourse per se, but neodiscourse. Therefore, the subject is contextualized into a semanticist paradigm of expression that includes consciousness as a whole. 

Your thoughts?
I think the view is existentialist. Obviously the predialiactric rationalism only applies to neosexists, to be pedantic. Postmodern culturalism has it that rationalism is merely judged by the view of the time, of what is acceptable. Since Smith didn't verbalise his groundings for his views, it may be argued that he is, in fact, irrational, presenting us with a completely different enigma of a sudorationalist paradigm.

### Post by stephantom on 2007-04-19
> **username132 said:**
> How come I can't load ubuntu.com but I can get a reply to a ping?
Because a ping is done on a lower network layer than HTTP (which is done on the top layer [application=7]). Something is overloaded/broken on one of the upper layers.

### Post by stefan1975 on 2007-04-19
> **tom56 said:**
> Out of interest - what's the difference betwen the two? I googled but everything's down :)

why download the dvd images at all? the installation is the same, it is just that there are more packages on the dvd (available in the official repo's as well, so you're not missing out with the cd), but apt-getting these will just download them from internet anyway giving you the latest and greatest version anyway. 

The dvd contains more packages and maybe more architectures, but i've never seen the use of it. I just down the x64 alternate install cd and install (x)ubuntu myself and apt-get what I'm missing.

### Post by xerosis on 2007-04-19
> **teutatis said:**
> If RC is the final why have they wait till 11 hours after gmt to update the server? why not bringing it up on time???

because it's not a case of pushing a button. they have to upload to the main server, and make sure it's on the numerous mirrors, and probably things we don't have a clue about. added to that, it makes sense to release it slightly later in the day GMT when server admins etc. will actually be working so they can make sure the servers don't fall over :)

### Post by dacha on 2007-04-19
> **Amorphous_Snake said:**
> 

But how do you check MD5?

cd to the directory with the file, put the MD5SUMS there, and type
$ md5sum --check MD5SUMS

### Post by elijahclarity on 2007-04-19
> **lionel47 said:**
> I am excited about the Feisty release.  I reinstalled Ubuntu a couple of weeks ago after about 18 months of not playing with Linux and was really impressed.  So far, I have been using Edgy as my primary desktop.  Unfortunately, because of M$'s refusal to use open document formats, I have to reboot into Windoze to write documents and presentations.  No matter what anyone says OO.Org and AbiWord just don't translate M$ Word and PowerPoint presentations correctly.

Having said that, has anyone had any success with Windows on a virtual machine?

Have you tried openSUSE 10.2's OpenOffice? If not, try it. You'll be AMAZED!:KS 
I don't know what openSUSE did to OO, but it has certainly made it GREATLY compatible with MS office documents. I had this CV of mine which was created in MS Word and never showed correctly in any distro's OO, until I tried openSUSE's OO. And I was ASTOUNDED. It almost seemed I was running MS Word! All the MS Word-specific tweaks, signs, formatting and stuff showed itself correctly and flawlessly!

### Post by keith11 on 2007-04-19
> **Dyegov said:**
> What are the differences between the CD image and the DVD image?

As far as I know (and very likely that's the case too), a CD will have just the basic installation and packages. If you install through a CD and if you have a good internet connection you can download all the other packages using one of the package managers in ubuntu/kubuntu. With a DVD, you will have those packages on the DVD and you can install them right at the time you are installing Ubuntu. A DVD is just sometimes better for me becuase my internet connection at home fluctuates so I prefer everything (of course not the daily updates) handy, on a DVD. But with respect to having access to packages and type of packages, there is no vital difference between a CD and a DVD of Ubuntu. Hope that helps.

Keith.

### Post by Sokraates on 2007-04-19
> **Dyegov said:**
> I have just seen some videos comparing Vista and Ubuntu with Beryl, and I have no words to describe how impresssd I am. Is it integrated with Feisty Fawn? Does it come with the CD iso image? Will it work with a 64mb integrated video card?

The effects are there, but not enabled by default. There's a tool called "Desktop Effects", where you can enable wobbly windows and the cube.

I don't have any experiance with 64MB. also it depends on what card you have. Intel and old ATIs are okay, since their open-source-drivers can display openGl-effects. With anything else, you will need the proprietary drivers, which you will have to download. 

For this, too, Feisty has a tool: Restricted Drivers Manager.

### Post by Sokraates on 2007-04-19

> Well, I won't get my hopes up too much. And if beryl is not final yet, then I won't use it. The one that comes with Feisty should be enough. I hope that one works for me . ..  Thanks for the advice ;)

Neither Compiz nor Beryl are final. Compiz is a bit more stable, but unfortunately won't work for everyone (it didn't for me). Beryl has more plugins and glitter, but many are not considered stable yet. Also Beryl may not work for everyone (it did for me thou). 

The projects are merging, so we will definitely have some excitement with Gutsy. Until then, just try both. You can get them from the Ubuntu-repositories but you can't have both installed at the same time.

### Post by bradweiser on 2007-04-19
> **XomboX said:**
> Guyzzz! How can I update to Feisty from Edgy using update-manager?

```
sudo update-manager -c -d
```

### Post by SonicSteve on 2007-04-19
This from the how to upgrade from Ubuntu says to upgrade from the "alternate" CD. Can you use the regular desktop CD also?

[SIZE="1"]Upgrading using the alternate CD/DVD

Use this method if the system being upgraded is not connected to the Internet.

   1.      Download and burn the alternate installation CD
   2.      Insert it into your CD-ROM drive
   3.      A dialog will be displayed offering you the opportunity to upgrade using that CD
   4.      Follow the on-screen instructions

If the upgrade dialog is not displayed for any reason, you may also run the following command using Alt+F2:

gksu "sh /cdrom/cdromupgrade" 

Note that for Kubuntu the upgrade dialogue will not be displayed and you will need to install gksu before running the above command (it will not work with kdesu). [/SIZE]

### Post by raul_ on 2007-04-19
> **Sokraates said:**
> If you wan to upgrade, start edgy and add the CD as a repository to Synaptic. Though upgrading was not possible with a Desktop-CD. I don't know if it's possible now.

> pgrading using the alternate CD/DVD

Use this method if the system being upgraded is not connected to the Internet.

   1.

      Download and burn the alternate installation CD
   2.

      Insert it into your CD-ROM drive
   3.

      A dialog will be displayed offering you the opportunity to upgrade using that CD
   4.

      Follow the on-screen instructions

If the upgrade dialog is not displayed for any reason, you may also run the following command using Alt+F2:

gksu "sh /cdrom/cdromupgrade" 

Note that for Kubuntu the upgrade dialogue will not be displayed and you will need to install gksu before running the above command (it will not work with kdesu). 

from [www.ubuntu.com](www.ubuntu.com)

### Post by NilsE on 2007-04-19
I have been a lurker and not much of a poster but I have to say I am thrilled with 7.04.

A first occurred, the X Server actually loaded without manipulation for the first time on my Dell D620 (Intel video chip).  It did not come up in native resolution but that is easy to fix with 915resolution. 

The reason that I am so thrilled is because that will make it much easier to get it installed on my external hard drive from the GUI install. Then I can fix the resolution and configure to my hearts content. Among other things in 7.04 this was a major step forward for me since I have never been able to run LiveCD with any version.

Love it.. Thanks

### Post by frodon on 2007-04-19
> **Gromit83 said:**
> I just want to cry. Feisty reckognizes my IDE drive as SCSI/S-ATA. So it crashes on GRUB ](*,)It's normal because IDE drives are now handled by the sata drivers, shouldn't be a problem if you use UUID instead of /dev/hdx location what should already the case if you never tweaked your fstab file.
Type this command to get the UUID of your drives :
```
sudo ls -l  /dev/disk/by-uuid/
```Then replace the /dev/hd location in your fstab by UUID=88140bc6-d24e- for example (replace the number by the UUID of your partition.

Do that and you are ready to go ;)

---

I like torrents so I went to the 6.10 torrent location, the erased the 6.10 from the end of the url, which takes me to a place where I can then pick on this link to get Xubuntu ([http://cdimage.ubuntu.com/](http://cdimage.ubuntu.com/))

HE HE HE. It'll be waiting for me when I get home. ANyone else who wants the wget command here ya go:
The Alternate Install CD:
wget httX://cdimage.ubuntu.com/xubuntu/releases/7.04/release/xubuntu-7.04-alternate-i386.iso
The Live CD:
wget httX://cdimage.ubuntu.com/xubuntu/releases/7.04/release/xubuntu-7.04-desktop-i386.iso

NOTE: AFTER COPYING AND PASTING, CHANGE 'X' TO 'the 'P' within http because it kept cutting the link down so a copy and paste wasn't working. Hopefully this will.

### Post by dangerpl on 2007-04-19
> **daygoj said:**
> OK PEOPLE DONT IGNORE ME how do i save as.......... when downloadin this thing

When you click on the link to the iso file a dialog will open giving you two options: Save As and Open with... something like that depending on the browser. Choose save as and save to desktop, when it downloads, right click and choose appropriate program to burn it. Don't use unpacking software, that will get you back to the initial problem...

---

### Post by phansiizwe on 2007-04-19
daygoj,

if you're downloading via firefox, then click on the link to the iso file with the right mouse button, then choose:

 Save Link As...

---

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-04-19
> **daygoj said:**
> wat!?

Maybe you should get some rest first.

When you click the link to download the .iso it opens a dialog box and asks you what you want to do. You have two options: open it (I think it defaults to file-roller), or save to disk. Don't open it. Select save to disk. When it finishes you will have a .iso on your desktop (or wherever you choose to save). Right click that and choose write to disc. Burn it slowly, reboot from CD, and install.

---

### Post by dannyboy79 on 2007-04-19
> **daygoj said:**
> OK PEOPLE DONT IGNORE ME how do i save as.......... when downloadin this thing


if you're already in linux, just use
wget
it's awesome. here are all the wget commands for each of the versions. (NOTE: i had to change the 'P' in HTTP because it kept shrinking the link down. After copy and pasting, change X to a p.) If you're working from a live cd, don't forget to cd to a mounted hard drive cause I don't know if your ram space can hold 600mb. These are all for i386 architecture, make sure you read whether 32bit or 64bit. They are all iso files of the cd EXCEPT Kubuntu, that's a dvd iso (4.3 gb).

Xubuntu Alternate CD-32bit
wget httX://cdimage.ubuntu.com/xubuntu/releases/7.04/release/xubuntu-7.04-alternate-i386.iso

Xubuntu Desktop CD-32bit
wget httX://cdimage.ubuntu.com/xubuntu/releases/7.04/release/xubuntu-7.04-desktop-i386.iso

Xubuntu Alternate CD-64bit
wget httX://cdimage.ubuntu.com/xubuntu/releases/7.04/release/xubuntu-7.04-alternate-amd64.iso

Xubuntu Desktop-64bit
wget httX://cdimage.ubuntu.com/xubuntu/releases/7.04/release/xubuntu-7.04-desktop-amd64.iso

Ubuntu Alternate CD-32bit
wget httX://releases.ubuntu.com/7.04/ubuntu-7.04-alternate-i386.iso

Ubuntu Desktop-32bit
wget httX://releases.ubuntu.com/7.04/ubuntu-7.04-desktop-i386.iso

Ubuntu Alternate CD-64bit
wget httX://releases.ubuntu.com/7.04/ubuntu-7.04-alternate-amd64.iso

Ubuntu Desktop-64bit
wget httX://releases.ubuntu.com/7.04/ubuntu-7.04-desktop-amd64.iso

Ubuntu Server-32bit
wget httX://releases.ubuntu.com/7.04/ubuntu-7.04-server-i386.iso

Ubuntu Server-64bit
wget httX://releases.ubuntu.com/7.04/ubuntu-7.04-server-amd64.iso

Kubuntu-64bit
wget httX://cdimage.ubuntu.com/kubuntu/releases/7.04/release/kubuntu-7.04-dvd-amd64.iso

Kubuntu-32bit
wget httX://cdimage.ubuntu.com/kubuntu/releases/7.04/release/kubuntu-7.04-dvd-i386.iso

### Post by thefoolisme on 2007-04-19
Ubuntu servers can't keep up with Demand!  Funny, I don't remember hearing anything close to this when VIsta came out...no long lines at stores...or anything  :-)

This just posted at zdnet.com:

Ubuntu 'Feisty Fawn' released, hit by traffic
By Stephen Shankland, CNET News.com 
Published on ZDNet News: April 19, 2007, 11:41 AM PT


Canonical on Thursday released version 7.04 of Ubuntu Linux, nicknamed Feisty Fawn, but the company's Web site was unable to keep up with the demand for the software. 

The up-and-coming Ubuntu has yet to attain the commercially blessed status of Red Hat Enterprise Linux and Novell's Suse Linux Enterprise, which have been in the marketplace years longer and are certified to work with many software and hardware products. But Canonical's software has built a significant fan base with its twice-yearly updates, user-friendly values and cutesy naming scheme. 

Feisty Fawn held up better than the protagonist in the animation Bambi Meets Godzilla: Canonical put up a bare-bones home page with just a single logo and a list of "mirror" sites from which the software can be downloaded. Still, the site was unavailable for more than half of the day, according to site availability monitoring company Pingdom. 

"We have been absolutely swamped with hits to the Web site and the mirrors," said Canonical Chief Executive Mark Shuttleworth in a conference call. "Fortunately there are 160 mirrors out there, all rapidly updating to include Feisty Fawn. We hope the logjam won't last much longer." 

Feisty Fawn features virtualization support, a new crash-reporting tool to aid debugging, but not the glitzy 3D interface Shuttleworth initially wanted. 

Ubuntu got an unsolicited endorsement from Michael Dell, chairman and CEO of Dell, a computer maker that's been wrestling with how to meet demand for desktop Linux. On Wednesday, the company announced on its Direct2Dell blog that Michael Dell got a new notebook with Feisty Fawn installed. 

Shuttleworth said he didn't talk to Dell's CEO about the move and wouldn't comment on whether he was in discussions with the computer maker for some sort of partnership. But Dell's move "does suggest that the company is forward-looking and perhaps considering Ubuntu," Shuttleworth said. 

Ubuntu is chiefly popular on PCs today, but Canonical is following the well-worn path to the server as it builds its Linux business. On servers, the open-source operating system is a stronger rival to Microsoft Windows and functionally very similar to versions of Unix that many administrators are familiar with. Red Hat and Novell's Linux business is chiefly from selling support subscriptions to server customers. 

Also on Thursday, Canonical announced a partnership with Sun Microsystems to bolster its server push. The company has integrated Sun's Java software with Feisty Fawn, making it available through the "multiverse" collection of preconfigured, downloadable software packages. 

Sun has begun making its core Java Standard Edition software open source and will finish during the first half of 2007, said Jeet Kaul, Sun's vice president of developer products and programs. Other components already are open-source software, including the Glassfish project for Java Enterprise Edition, a collection of extensions for running Java on servers, and NetBeans, a Java programming environment. 

Java SE, Glassfish and NetBeans all are available for Feisty Fawn, Shuttleworth said. 

"This is the first time the Java platform technology has been fully integrated into a Linux distribution to this extent," said Ian Murdock, Sun's newly appointed chief operating systems officer and founder of the Debian version of Linux on which Ubuntu is based. 

Though NetBeans is his own "preferred Java development environment," Shuttleworth said that its main rival, Eclipse, already is integrated into Ubuntu. 

The next version of Ubuntu, Gutsy Gibbon, is due in October. Neither it nor Feisty Fawn features the long-term support of version 6.06, called Dapper Drake. A version with long-term support, which lasts five years, likely won't arrive until the release of Gutsy Gibbon's successor, Shuttleworth said.

### Post by neatojones on 2007-04-19
> **Immolatus said:**
> hello all,
I just finished install of feisty.....for what ever reason the "cube" effect wont work but the windows wobble just fine ....any thoughts?

Couple of things could be going on
Open gconf-editor and then:
set /apps/compiz/general/screen0/options/hsize  "4"

If it still doesn't work then:
right click /apps/compiz/general/allscreens/options/active_plugins and select "unset key"

### Post by DXR on 2007-04-19
I was gonna wait a few days to update through the update manager cause I knew the server was being hammered, but i couldn't wait to try it out! Took like 4-5 hours to download the packages, another hour for the upgrade to take place, now it's up running \\:D/ 

Unfortunately, not everything was ok after i rebooted. X died on me after logging in, I WAS expecting tha though. I had beryl installed on edgy so I had to remove it in the virtual terminal and replace nvidia with nv in xorg.conf. I tried to use the new bult-in restricted drivers installer but it kept telling me that my hardware does not need restricted drivers :confused: 

Anyway, i tried to enable Desktop-Effects (Compiz) in case that enabled the need for the Nvidia drivers but no luck. So i finally installed envy and got the nvidia drivers. Now X is running perfectly and i got beryl back :mrgreen: 

Besides some wine related icons that filled the menu launcher everything is going well. Thumbs up to the developers =D>

### Post by JeevesBond on 2007-04-19
[quote=rabid]where are you downloading from?[/quote]
He's downloading from bittorrent which means he's downloading from everyone else who's using Bittorrent. It's a peer-to-peer thingamy. :)

Just pick a server at [http://www.ubuntu.com](http://www.ubuntu.com) pick the download you want, but instead of getting the ISO you want the .torrent file. You'll also need a bittorrent client (I use the [Opera browser](http://www.opera.com) which has one built-in). If you open that .torrent file in Opera (or some bittorrent client) it'll start downloading!

Hope this helps. :)

What's the easiest, most reliable way to upgrade from Edgy to Feisty?   What is likely to give me the least trouble in other words with all of the repositories, etc.    I can't handle everything breaking again and going thru the whole re-install mess.   Edgy is working so smoothly now ...

### Post by FuturePilot on 2007-04-19

### Post by smartalecks on 2007-04-19
> **myke said:**
> OK ... I like to keep up with the latest versions ... I can't help it.   But ... I had a horrible time upgrading from Dapper to Edgy and ended up having to reinstall both my Kubuntu & XP partitions from scratch as everything was such a mess.   

What's the easiest, most reliable way to upgrade from Edgy to Feisty?   What is likely to give me the least trouble in other words with all of the repositories, etc.    I can't handle everything breaking again and going thru the whole re-install mess.   Edgy is working so smoothly now ...

Navigate to: **System** > **Administration** > [B][U]Update Manager
[/U][/B]
[IMG]http://i11.tinypic.com/44hzub8.jpg[/IMG]

Then hit "**Upgrade**." It'll take a while to download and then to install, but that's the official, and in my experience, best way.

**Notes:**
- Be careful if you have a composite manager (Beryl, Compiz) or custom configurations to Xorg. An upgrade will probably break whatever they are, and you are better off with a clean install (so back up alot).
- You might want to try on the weekend when the servers aren't being hammered so hard by others trying to upgrade.

Or, just back everything up and do a fresh install.

---

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-04-19
> **Mazza558 said:**
> Surely someone else out there has had this problem?

You should post that question is a support thread. This thread is moving fast enough that not many people are going to see it and even fewer who know the answer.

However, this might help. Since it says it's already mounted do
```
sudo umount /path/to/mount/point
sudo mount /dev/sda2 /path/to/mount/point
```
Linux doesn't need a type switch for a Linux FS (or maybe it's just Ubuntu not needing it for an ext3 - I'm not sure but I've never used one).

### Post by Ace2016 on 2007-04-19
> **Mazza558 said:**
> By terminal it tells me "device is busy"
By GUI it tells me "device does no agree with the fstab"

Yea the release is a bit messed up, i installed with the beta alternative installer and it detected by ide disks as scsi for some reason, and indicated they were /dev/da* instead of being /dev/hd*, i had to edit my fstab myself and correct it, i got rid of the UUIDs since i can't remember a random string of junk but i can remember /dev/hda6

So you should run:

cd /dev/
ls hd*

This will show what drives you have, now pick the one you want and mount it

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-04-19
> **Mazza558 said:**
> I've narrowed it down to permissions - if there a way to give a whole drive permissions like this? Some of my folders on there have locked symbols next to them whilst others don't -  I've been messing with chown commands)

I don't know if there is a switch to mount with different permissions but if you mount with sudo (and I think you have to), it may give root permission to anything that it can't identify permissions for. I know my backup drive has root permissions except on the files backed up from my /home. I suppose you could chown everything. What are you using the drive for? If it's for your files I don't see why this would be an issue. If you save something there it will have your permissions (unless you were doing as root).

As much as I like keeping this thread alive, you really should post your question in a support forum. Right now you are only getting help from one dumb a** (me). You would have more exposure and better luck in a support forum.

Then hit "**Upgrade**." It'll take a while to download and then to install, but that's the official, and in my experience, best way.

**Notes:**
- Be careful if you have a composite manager (Beryl, Compiz) or custom configurations to Xorg. An upgrade will probably break whatever they are, and you are better off with a clean install (so back up alot).
- You might want to try on the weekend when the servers aren't being hammered so hard by others trying to upgrade.

Or, just back everything up and do a fresh install.

Thank you fo this useful post!

Just one question:

I'm on beryl. Does that mean i'm gonna have to reinstall everything? all my settings, emerald themes, skydomes?? eek..

Abort, abort!! How do I cancel a Upgrade (that has been going for 10 hours and is only 50% done dowonloading)?

### Post by maniacmusician on 2007-04-19
> **SaddaGocaraRupa said:**
> Thank you fo this useful post!

Just one question:

I'm on beryl. Does that mean i'm gonna have to reinstall everything? all my settings, emerald themes, skydomes?? eek..

Abort, abort!! How do I cancel a Upgrade (that has been going for 10 hours and is only 50% done dowonloading)?
you won't lose all your beryl settings. Just back up your ~/.beryl and ~/.emerald folders (thats where all your settings are).  

You probably **will** break your Beryl installation. which means you'll have to completely remove beryl, and then reinstall it for Feisty Fawn. Other than that, you probably won't have trouble with much else, hopefully.

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2007-04-20
> **daygoj said:**
> fiesty feisty fiesty,YES ok now how do i install wine for fiesty

No need to get automatix for wine sake.

```
wget -q http://wine.budgetdedicated.com/apt/387EE263.gpg -O- | sudo apt-key add -
sudo wget http://wine.budgetdedicated.com/apt/sources.list.d/feisty.list -O /etc/apt/sources.list.d/winehq.list
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install wine
```

Note: It's for x86

for 64 bit users: [http://wiki.winehq.org/UbuntuAMD64](http://wiki.winehq.org/UbuntuAMD64)

---

### Post by pepsi_max2k on 2007-04-22
>>I believe the desktop effects are done by Compiz. Use beryl instead =P.

That's what I've done. With an Nvidia card it's simple, just search for "compiz" in synaptic, get rid of anything that comes up, then search for "beryl", "beryl-manager" and "emerald" and that should install everything you need. Open Beryl Manager, right click the taskbar icon and chose Beryl from Select Windows Manager. Done.

### Post by raul_ on 2007-04-24
> **m.musashi said:**
> BTW, shouldn't gutsy have been the Gnarley Gnu (a gnu is an antelope type animal and it's pronounced "new"). It was a great opportunity for some GNU wordplay. And I'm too thrilled to say gutsy over and over. It doesn't roll the same way as feisty or edgy.

> The Gibbon won the G-race to be our engineering mascot for this next
release, but it was a close run. We very much wanted to honour the
tremendous contributions of the GNU project to Free Software by awarding
the role to the Glossy Gnu. This prompted an intense internal debate
about trademarks, at which both the Fiery Fox and the Icy Weasel were
heard. In the end, however, the judge, jury and elocutionary (that would
be me) took a liking to the Gibbon's extraordinary reach, and the Gibbon
won outright.

The Glossy Gnu will nonetheless play a role in this next release,
because Ubuntu 7.10 will feature a new flavour - as yet unnamed - which
takes an ultra-orthodox view of licensing: no firmware, drivers,
imagery, sounds, applications, or other content which do not include
full source materials and come with full rights of modification,
remixing and redistribution. There should be no more conservative home,
for those who demand a super-strict interpretation of the "free" in free
software. This work will be done in collaboration with the folks behind
Gnewsense.

from [https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-devel-announce/2007-April/000276.html]("https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-devel-announce/2007-April/000276.html")

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-04-24
> **Efros said:**
> Got Beryl working very nice, wonder if there's a script to automate it kinda like a screensaver. found that the use of compiz and/or beryl will mess up any rdc or vnc access to your desktop though. Wonder if theres an alternative.

What do you mean by automate? If you just want it to autostart when you log in, you can go to -> System -> Preferences -> Sessions ->new and then Name = Beryl and Command = beryl-manager (from memory - not on Ubuntu at the moment). Sometimes autostart happens too soon (at least I had problems but that was back in Dapper) so you could also use a little bash script to start it after a delay. I'm not 100% sure but maybe something like
```
#!/bin/bash
sleep 10 && beryl-manager;
```
Name it .beryl_start.sh and chmod it
```
chmod a+x .beryl_start.sh
```
and add it to the start up (use the full path to the command).

---

I downloaded & burned Feisty Fawn a few days ago.  I'm running on Ubuntu (desktop) right now, couldn't be happier.

However, I tried to install Xubuntu (alternate) to my "Low Memory" 64_MB antique laptop (HP Pavilion N3270, not that it matters here), and there were just 'way too many choices early in the install, things that I had to guess at, and with no clue as to their importance.  One screen of guessing wasn't too bad, but multiple ones were over the top.  So I went back to the same in Dapper Drake, no special questions there and it went on just fine.
